    24	/** @internal JIT-compiled hydrator that converts raw database rows into entity instances with optimized generated code. */
    25	export class ObjectHydrator extends Hydrator {
    26	  readonly #hydrators = {
    27	    'full~true': new Map<EntityName, EntityHydrator<any>>(),
    28	    'full~false': new Map<EntityName, EntityHydrator<any>>(),
    29	    'reference~true': new Map<EntityName, EntityHydrator<any>>(),
    30	    'reference~false': new Map<EntityName, EntityHydrator<any>>(),
    31	  };
    32	
    33	  #tmpIndex = 0;
    34	
    35	  /**
    36	   * @inheritDoc
    37	   */
    38	  override hydrate<T extends object>(
    39	    entity: T,
    40	    meta: EntityMetadata<T>,
    41	    data: EntityData<T>,
    42	    factory: EntityFactory,
    43	    type: 'full' | 'reference',

    48	    normalizeAccessors?: boolean,
    49	  ): void {
    50	    const hydrate = this.getEntityHydrator(meta, type, normalizeAccessors);
    51	    const running = this.running;
    52	    // the running state is used to consider propagation as hydration, saving the values directly to the entity data,
    53	    // but we don't want that for new entities, their propagation should result in entity updates when flushing
    54	    this.running = !newEntity;
    55	    Utils.callCompiledFunction(
    56	      hydrate,
    57	      entity,
    58	      data,
    59	      factory,
    60	      newEntity,
    61	      convertCustomTypes,

    63	      parentSchema,
    64	      normalizeAccessors,
    65	    );
    66	    this.running = running;
    67	  }

    69	  /**
    70	   * @inheritDoc
    71	   */
    72	  override hydrateReference<T extends object>(
    73	    entity: T,
    74	    meta: EntityMetadata<T>,

   102	  getEntityHydrator<T extends object>(
   103	    meta: EntityMetadata<T>,
   104	    type: 'full' | 'reference',
   105	    normalizeAccessors = false,
   106	  ): EntityHydrator<T> {
   107	    const key = `${type}~${normalizeAccessors}` as const;
   108	    const exists = this.#hydrators[key].get(meta.class);
   109	
   110	    if (exists) {
   111	      return exists;
   112	    }
   113	
   114	    const lines: string[] = [];
   115	    const context = new Map<string, any>();
   116	    const props = this.getProperties(meta, type);
   117	    context.set('isPrimaryKey', Utils.isPrimaryKey);
   118	    context.set('isEntity', EntityHelper.isEntity);
   119	    context.set('isScalarReference', ScalarReference.isScalarReference);
   120	    context.set('Collection', Collection);
   121	    context.set('Reference', Reference);
   122	    context.set('PolymorphicRef', PolymorphicRef);
   123	    context.set('ValidationError', ValidationError);
   124	
   125	    const registerCustomType = <T>(
   126	      prop: EntityProperty<T>,
   127	      convertorKey: string,
   128	      method: 'convertToDatabaseValue' | 'convertToJSValue',
   129	      context: Map<string, any>,
   130	    ) => {
   131	      context.set(`${method}_${convertorKey}`, (val: any) => {
   132	        /* v8 ignore next */
   133	        if (Raw.isKnownFragment(val)) {
   134	          return val;
   135	        }
   136	
   137	        return prop.customType![method](val, this.platform, { mode: 'serialization' });
   138	      });
   139	
   140	      return convertorKey;
   141	    };
   142	
   143	    const hydrateScalar = (prop: EntityProperty<T>, path: string[], dataKey: string): string[] => {
   144	      const entityKey = path.map(k => this.wrap(k)).join('');
   145	      const tz = this.platform.getTimezone();
   146	      const convertorKey = path
   147	        .filter(k => !/\[idx_\d+]/.exec(k))
   148	        .map(k => this.safeKey(k))
   149	        .join('_');
   150	      const ret: string[] = [];
   151	      const idx = this.#tmpIndex++;
   152	      const nullVal = this.config.get('forceUndefined') ? 'undefined' : 'null';
   153	
   154	      if (prop.getter && !prop.setter && prop.persist === false) {
   155	        return [];
   156	      }
   157	
   158	      if (prop.ref) {
   159	        context.set('ScalarReference', ScalarReference);
   160	        ret.push(`  const oldValue_${idx} = entity${entityKey};`);
   161	      }
   162	
   163	      ret.push(`  if (data${dataKey} === null) {`);
   164	      if (prop.ref) {
   165	        ret.push(`    entity${entityKey} = new ScalarReference();`);
   166	        ret.push(`    entity${entityKey}.bind(entity, '${prop.name}');`);
   167	        ret.push(`    entity${entityKey}.set(${nullVal});`);
   168	      } else {
   169	        ret.push(`    entity${entityKey} = ${nullVal};`);
   170	      }
   171	      ret.push(`  } else if (typeof data${dataKey} !== 'undefined') {`);
   172	
   173	      if (prop.customType) {
   174	        registerCustomType(prop, convertorKey, 'convertToJSValue', context);
   175	        registerCustomType(prop, convertorKey, 'convertToDatabaseValue', context);
   176	
   177	        ret.push(

   179	          `      const value = convertToJSValue_${convertorKey}(data${dataKey});`,
   180	        );
   181	
   182	        if (prop.customType.ensureComparable(meta, prop)) {
   183	          ret.push(`      data${dataKey} = convertToDatabaseValue_${convertorKey}(value);`);
   184	        }
   185	
   186	        ret.push(
   187	          `      entity${entityKey} = value;`,
   188	          `    } else {`,
   189	          `      entity${entityKey} = data${dataKey};`,
   190	          `    }`,
   191	        );
   192	      } else if (prop.runtimeType === 'boolean') {
   193	        ret.push(`    entity${entityKey} = !!data${dataKey};`);
   194	      } else if (prop.runtimeType === 'Date' && !this.platform.isNumericProperty(prop)) {
   195	        ret.push(`    if (data${dataKey} instanceof Date) {`);
   196	        ret.push(`      entity${entityKey} = data${dataKey};`);
   197	
   198	        if (!tz || tz === 'local') {
   199	          ret.push(`    } else {`);
   200	          ret.push(`      entity${entityKey} = new Date(data${dataKey});`);
   201	        } else {
   202	          ret.push(

   205	          ret.push(`      entity${entityKey} = new Date(data${dataKey});`);
   206	          ret.push(`    } else {`);
   207	          ret.push(`      entity${entityKey} = new Date(data${dataKey} + '${tz}');`);
   208	        }
   209	
   210	        ret.push(`    }`);
   211	      } else {
   212	        ret.push(`    entity${entityKey} = data${dataKey};`);
   213	      }
   214

   216	        ret.push(
   217	          `    const value = isScalarReference(entity${entityKey}) ? entity${entityKey}.unwrap() : entity${entityKey};`,

   219	        ret.push(`    entity${entityKey} = oldValue_${idx} ?? new ScalarReference(value);`);
   220	        ret.push(`    entity${entityKey}.bind(entity, '${prop.name}');`);

   226	      if (prop.ref) {


But notice that for the non-recursive case (line 414), it uses `this.wrap(p.name)` to get the data key. However, for nested embeddables (when `p.kind === ReferenceKind.EMBEDDED && !p.object && !p.array`), it recurses with `dataKey + this.wrap(p.embedded![1])`.

The problem is: when checking if the parent is null (line 507), it calls `createCond(prop, dataKey, '=== null')`. Now I see the issue clearly. Let me trace through the logic.

In `createCond` (line 399-419):
- For an inline (non-object) embeddable, it filters `meta.props` for properties where `p.embedded?.[0] === prop.name`
- For each child property, if it's an embedded (non-object, non-array), it recurses with `dataKey + this.wrap(p.embedded![1])`
- Otherwise, it uses `this.wrap(p.name)` to build the condition

But in `hydrateEmbedded` (line 421-514), when building the actual hydration code:
- For inline embeddables, it builds `embeddedData` using `this.wrap(childProp.name)` (line 437)
- When recursing into children (lines 488-498), it passes `prop.object` to `hydrateProperty`, which determines the dataKey

The problem is that `createCond` builds data keys differently than `hydrateProperty` for nested inline embeddables.

Let me look at how `hydrateProperty` constructs dataKey for inline (non-object) child properties:

Looking at line 540-541:
```ts
dataKey = dataKey ?? (object ? entityKey : this.wrap(normalizeAccessors ? (prop.accessor ?? prop.name) : prop.name));
```

For top-level inline embeddable, `object` is false, so `dataKey = this.wrap(prop.name)`.

In `hydrateEmbedded` at line 491:
```ts
const childDataKey = prop.object ? dataKey + this.wrap(childProp.embedded![1]) : this.wrap(childProp.name);
```

But in `createCond` at line 410:
```ts
conds.push(...createCond(p, dataKey + this.wrap(p.embedded![1]), cond));
```

And at line 414:
```ts
conds.push(`data${this.wrap(p.name)} ${notNull}`);
```

So `createCond` for a nested inline embeddable (where `p` is the child embedded property) uses `dataKey + this.wrap(p.embedded![1])` to recurse. But that's the path-based approach. Then at the leaf level, it uses `this.wrap(p.name)`.

Wait, let me think about this more carefully. For a nested inline embeddable like:

```
ParentEntity
  -> embeddable1 (inline)
    -> embeddable2 (inline)
      -> field1
```

When hydrating, the data keys would be:
- For `embeddable1`: `this.wrap('embeddable1')` e.g., `['embeddable1']`
- For `embeddable2` inside embeddable1: `this.wrap('embeddable2')` e.g., `['embeddable2']` (NOT `['embeddable1']['embeddable2']`)

Because `prop.object` is false at line 491, so `childDataKey = this.wrap(childProp.name)`.

But in `createCond`:
- For the first level (embeddable1), it filters `meta.props` for `p.embedded?.[0] === 'embeddable1'`
- For a child that is also an inline embeddable (embeddable2), it recurses with `dataKey + this.wrap(p.embedded![1])` which would be `'' + this.wrap('embeddable2')` = `['embeddable2']`
- For a leaf scalar in embeddable2, it would use `this.wrap(p.name)` i.e., `['field1']`

So this actually seems consistent! Both use the same flat column naming.

Let me reconsider. Maybe the issue is different. Let me look at the actual test files related to this issue.

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/repro.ts << 'EOF'
import { MikroORM } from '@mikro-orm/sqlite';
import { Embeddable, Embedded, Entity, PrimaryKey, Property, ReflectMetadataProvider } from '@mikro-orm/decorators/legacy';

@Embeddable()
class NestedMeta {
  @Property({ nullable: true })
  foo?: string;

  constructor(foo?: string) {
    this.foo = foo;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class ParentMeta {
  @Embedded(() => NestedMeta, { nullable: true })
  nested?: NestedMeta;

  constructor(nested?: NestedMeta) {
    this.nested = nested;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class Identity {
  @Property()
  email!: string;

  @Embedded(() => ParentMeta, { nullable: true })
  parent?: ParentMeta;

  constructor(email: string, parent?: ParentMeta) {
    this.email = email;
    this.parent = parent;
  }
}

@Entity()
class User {
  @PrimaryKey()
  id!: number;

  @Property()
  name!: string;

  @Embedded(() => Identity)
  identity!: Identity;
}

async function main() {
  const orm = await MikroORM.init({
    metadataProvider: ReflectMetadataProvider,
    entities: [User],
    dbName: ':memory:',
    forceUndefined: true,
  });
  
  await orm.schema.createSchema();
  
  // Case 1: parent is set, nested is set
  const user1 = new User();
  user1.name = 'Test1';
  user1.identity = new Identity('email1@test.com', new ParentMeta(new NestedMeta('bar')));
  await orm.em.persist(user1).flush();
  console.log('User 1 saved with ID:', user1.id);
  
  // Case 2: parent is null, nested is effectively null
  const user2 = new User();
  user2.name = 'Test2';
  user2.identity = new Identity('email2@test.com', null);
  await orm.em.persist(user2).flush();
  console.log('User 2 saved with ID:', user2.id);
  
  // Case 3: parent is set but nested is null
  const user3 = new User();
  user3.name = 'Test3';
  user3.identity = new Identity('email3@test.com', new ParentMeta(null));
  await orm.em.persist(user3).flush();
  console.log('User 3 saved with ID:', user3.id);
  
  orm.em.clear();
  
  // Now read them back
  const users = await orm.em.findAll(User);
  for (const u of users) {
    console.log(`User ${u.id}: name=${u.name}, identity.email=${u.identity.email}, parent=${JSON.stringify(u.identity.parent)}, nested=${JSON.stringify(u.identity.parent?.nested)}`);
  }
  
  await orm.close();
}

main().catch(console.error);

Let me verify this by looking at the `createCond` function again:

```ts
const createCond = (prop: EntityProperty, dataKey: string, cond?: string) => {
    const conds: string[] = [];

    if (prop.object) {
        conds.push(`data${dataKey} ${cond ?? '!= null'}`);
    } else {
        const notNull = cond ?? (prop.nullable ? '!= null' : '!== undefined');
        meta.props
            .filter(p => p.embedded?.[0] === prop.name)
            .forEach(p => {
                if (p.kind === ReferenceKind.EMBEDDED && !p.object && !p.array) {
                    conds.push(...createCond(p, dataKey + this.wrap(p.embedded![1]), cond));
                    return;
                }

                conds.push(`data${this.wrap(p.name)} ${notNull}`);
            });
    }

    return conds;
};
```

```ts
conds.push(...createCond(p, dataKey + this.wrap(p.embedded![1]), cond));
```

Here, `p.embedded![1]` is the short name (e.g., `'parent'`), and `dataKey` is the path from parent (e.g., `['identity']`). So the new `dataKey` becomes `['identity']['parent']`.

```ts
const isParentObject: (prop: EntityProperty) => boolean = (prop: EntityProperty) => {
```

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/repro2.ts << 'EOF'
import { MikroORM } from '@mikro-orm/sqlite';
import {
  Embeddable,
  Embedded,
  Entity,
  PrimaryKey,
  Property,
  ReflectMetadataProvider,
} from '@mikro-orm/decorators/legacy';

@Embeddable()
class NestedMeta {
  @Property({ nullable: true })
  foo?: string;

  constructor(foo?: string) {
    this.foo = foo;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class ParentMeta {
  @Embedded(() => NestedMeta, { nullable: true })
  nested?: NestedMeta;

  constructor(nested?: NestedMeta) {
    this.nested = nested;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class Identity {
  @Property()
  email!: string;

  @Embedded(() => ParentMeta, { nullable: true })
  parent?: ParentMeta;

  constructor(email: string, parent?: ParentMeta) {
    this.email = email;
    this.parent = parent;
  }
}

@Entity()
class User {
  @PrimaryKey()
  id!: number;

  @Property()
  name!: string;

  @Embedded(() => Identity)
  identity!: Identity;
}

async function main() {
  const orm = await MikroORM.init({
    metadataProvider: ReflectMetadataProvider,
    entities: [User],
    dbName: ':memory:',
    forceUndefined: true,
  });
  
  await orm.schema.create();
  
  // Case 1: parent is set, nested is set
  const user1 = new User();
  user1.name = 'Test1';
  user1.identity = new Identity('email1@test.com', new ParentMeta(new NestedMeta('bar')));
  await orm.em.persist(user1).flush();
  console.log('User 1 saved with ID:', user1.id);
  
  // Case 2: parent is null
  const user2 = new User();
  user2.name = 'Test2';
  user2.identity = new Identity('email2@test.com', null);
  await orm.em.persist(user2).flush();
  console.log('User 2 saved with ID:', user2.id);
  
  // Case 3: parent is set but nested is null
  const user3 = new User();
  user3.name = 'Test3';
  user3.identity = new Identity('email3@test.com', new ParentMeta(null));
  await orm.em.persist(user3).flush();
  console.log('User 3 saved with ID:', user3.id);
  
  orm.em.clear();
  
  // Now read them back
  const users = await orm.em.findAll(User);
  for (const u of users) {
    console.log(`User ${u.id}: name=${u.name}, identity.email=${u.identity.email}, parent=${JSON.stringify(u.identity.parent)}, nested=${JSON.stringify(u.identity.parent?.nested)}`);
  }
  
  await orm.close();
  console.log('SUCCESS');
}

main().catch(e => {
  console.error('ERROR:', e.message);
  process.exit(1);
});
EOF

import { MikroORM } from '@mikro-orm/sqlite';
import {
  Embeddable,
  Embedded,
  Entity,
  PrimaryKey,
  Property,
  ReflectMetadataProvider,
} from '@mikro-orm/decorators/legacy';

@Embeddable()
class NestedMeta {
  @Property({ nullable: true })
  foo?: string;

  constructor(foo?: string) {
    this.foo = foo;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class ParentMeta {
  @Embedded(() => NestedMeta, { nullable: true })
  nested?: NestedMeta;

  constructor(nested?: NestedMeta) {
    this.nested = nested;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class Identity {
  @Property()
  email!: string;

  @Embedded(() => ParentMeta, { nullable: true })
  parent?: ParentMeta;

  constructor(email: string, parent?: ParentMeta) {
    this.email = email;
    this.parent = parent;
  }
}

@Entity()
class User {
  @PrimaryKey()
  id!: number;

  @Property()
  name!: string;

  @Embedded(() => Identity)
  identity!: Identity;
}

let orm: MikroORM;

beforeAll(async () => {
  orm = await MikroORM.init({
    metadataProvider: ReflectMetadataProvider,
    entities: [User],
    dbName: ':memory:',
    forceUndefined: true,
  });
  await orm.schema.create();
});

afterAll(async () => {
  await orm.close(true);
});

test('nested inline embeddable with null parent', async () => {
  // Case 1: parent is set, nested is set
  const user1 = new User();
  user1.name = 'Test1';
  user1.identity = new Identity('email1@test.com', new ParentMeta(new NestedMeta('bar')));
  await orm.em.persist(user1).flush();
  console.log('User 1 saved with ID:', user1.id);
  
  // Case 2: parent is null
  const user2 = new User();
  user2.name = 'Test2';
  user2.identity = new Identity('email2@test.com', null);
  await orm.em.persist(user2).flush();
  console.log('User 2 saved with ID:', user2.id);
  
  // Case 3: parent is set but nested is null
  const user3 = new User();
  user3.name = 'Test3';
  user3.identity = new Identity('email3@test.com', new ParentMeta(null));
  await orm.em.persist(user3).flush();
  console.log('User 3 saved with ID:', user3.id);
  
  orm.em.clear();
  
  // Now read them back
  const users = await orm.em.findAll(User);
  for (const u of users) {
    console.log(`User ${u.id}: name=${u.name}, identity.email=${u.identity.email}, parent=${JSON.stringify(u.identity.parent)}, nested=${JSON.stringify(u.identity.parent?.nested)}`);
  }
  
  expect(users[0].identity.parent).toBeDefined();
  expect(users[0].identity.parent!.nested).toBeDefined();
  expect(users[0].identity.parent!.nested!.foo).toBe('bar');
  
  expect(users[1].identity.parent).toBeNull();
  
  expect(users[2].identity.parent).toBeDefined();
  expect(users[2].identity.parent!.nested).toBeNull();
});

cd /testbed && cat > tests/repro2.test.ts << 'EOF'
import { MikroORM } from '@mikro-orm/sqlite';
import {
  Embeddable,
  Embedded,
  Entity,
  PrimaryKey,
  Property,
  ReflectMetadataProvider,
} from '@mikro-orm/decorators/legacy';

@Embeddable()
class NestedMeta {
  @Property({ nullable: true })
  foo?: string;

  constructor(foo?: string) {
    this.foo = foo;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class ParentMeta {
  @Embedded(() => NestedMeta, { nullable: true })
  nested?: NestedMeta;

  constructor(nested?: NestedMeta) {
    this.nested = nested;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class Identity {
  @Property()
  email!: string;

  @Embedded(() => ParentMeta, { nullable: true })
  parent?: ParentMeta;

  constructor(email: string, parent?: ParentMeta) {
    this.email = email;
    this.parent = parent;
  }
}

@Entity()
class User {
  @PrimaryKey()
  id!: number;

  @Property()
  name!: string;

  @Embedded(() => Identity)
  identity!: Identity;
}

let orm: MikroORM;

beforeAll(async () => {
  orm = await MikroORM.init({
    metadataProvider: ReflectMetadataProvider,
    entities: [User],
    dbName: ':memory:',
    forceUndefined: true,
  });
  await orm.schema.create();
});

afterAll(async () => {
  await orm.close(true);
});

test('debug', async () => {
  // Print metadata
  const meta = orm.getMetadata().get(User);
  for (const [key, prop] of Object.entries(meta.properties)) {
    console.log(`${key}: kind=${prop.kind}, embedded=${JSON.stringify(prop.embedded)}, object=${prop.object}, nullable=${prop.nullable}, fieldNames=${JSON.stringify(prop.fieldNames)}`);
  }
  
  const createSQL = await orm.schema.getCreateSchemaSQL({ wrap: false });
  console.log('Create SQL:');
  console.log(createSQL);
});
EOF

   605	  private processProperty<T extends object>(changeSet: ChangeSet<T>, prop: EntityProperty<T>): void {
   606	    const meta = changeSet.meta;
   607	    const value = changeSet.payload[prop.name] as unknown; // for inline embeddables
   608	
   609	    if (value instanceof EntityIdentifier) {
   610	      changeSet.payload[prop.name] = value.getValue();
   611	      return;
   612	    }
   613	
   614	    if (value instanceof PolymorphicRef) {
   615	      if (value.id instanceof EntityIdentifier) {
   616	        value.id = value.id.getValue();
   617	      }
   618	      return;
   619	    }
   620	
   621	    if (Array.isArray(value) && value.every(item => item instanceof EntityIdentifier)) {
   622	      changeSet.payload[prop.name] = value.map(item => item.getValue());

   624	    }
   625	
   626	    if (prop.kind === ReferenceKind.MANY_TO_MANY && Array.isArray(value)) {

   628	      return;

   630

   632	      return;
   633	    }
   634

   636	
   637	    values.forEach(([value, indexes]) => {
   638	      if (value instanceof EntityIdentifier) {
   639	        Utils.setPayloadProperty<T>(changeSet.payload, meta, prop, value.getValue(), indexes);

   303	      prop.embedded ? getRootProperty(meta.properties[prop.embedded[0] as EntityKey<T>]) : prop;
   304	
   305	    // copy all comparable props, ignore collections and references, process custom types
   306	    meta.comparableProps
   307	      .filter(prop => {
   308	        const root = getRootProperty(prop);
   309	        return prop === root || root.kind !== ReferenceKind.EMBEDDED;
   310	      })
   311	      .forEach(prop =>
   312	        lines.push(
   313	          this.getPropertySnapshot(meta, prop, context, this.wrap(prop.name), this.wrap(prop.name), [prop.name]),
   314	        ),
   315	      );
   316	
   317	    const code = `return function(entity) {\n  const ret = {};\n${lines.join('\n')}\n  return ret;\n}`;
   318	    const fnKey = `snapshotGenerator-${meta.uniqueName}`;
   319	    const snapshotGenerator = Utils.createFunction(context, code, this.#config?.get('compiledFunctions'), fnKey);
   320	    this.#snapshotGenerators.set(meta, snapshotGenerator);
   321	
   322	    return snapshotGenerator;
   323	  }
   324	
   325	  /**
   326	   * @internal
   327	   */
   328	  propName(name: string, parent = 'result'): string {
   329	    return parent + this.wrap(name);
   330	  }
   331	
   332	  /**
   333	   * @internal respects nested composite keys, e.g. `[1, [2, 3]]`
   334	   */
   335	  createCompositeKeyArray(prop: EntityProperty, parents: EntityProperty[] = []): string {
   336	    if (!prop.targetMeta) {
   337	      let fieldName = prop.fieldNames[0];
   338	      // traverse all parents, mapping my field name to each parent's field name until we reach the root
   339	      for (let i = parents.length - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
   340	        const parent = parents[i];
   341	
   342	        // skip m:n since it does not represent any column directly
   343	        if (parent.pivotEntity) {
   344	          continue;
   345	        }
   346	
   347	        const idx = parent.referencedColumnNames.indexOf(fieldName);
   348	        fieldName = parent.fieldNames[idx];
   349	      }
   350	
   351	      return this.propName(fieldName);
   352	    }
   353	
   354	    const parts: CompositeKeyPart[] = [];
   355	
   356	    prop.targetMeta.getPrimaryProps().forEach(pk => {
   357	      const part = this.createCompositeKeyArray(pk, [...parents, prop]);
   358	      parts.push(part);
   359	    });
   360	
   361	    return this.formatCompositeKeyPart(parts);
   362	  }
   363	
   364	  /**
   365	   * @internal
   366	   */
   367	  formatCompositeKeyPart(part: CompositeKeyPart): string {
   368	    if (!Array.isArray(part)) {
   369	      return part;
   370	    }
   371	
   372	    if (part.length === 1) {
   373	      return this.formatCompositeKeyPart(part[0]);
   374	    }
   375	
   376	    const formatted = part.map(p => this.formatCompositeKeyPart(p)).join(', ');
   377	    return `[${formatted}]`;
   378	  }
   379	
   380	  /**
   381	   * @internal Highly performance-sensitive method.
   382	   */
   383	  getResultMapper<T>(meta: EntityMetadata<T>): ResultMapper<T> {
   384	    const exists = this.#mappers.get(meta);
   385	
   386	    if (exists) {
   387	      return exists;
   388	    }
   389	
   390	    const lines: string[] = [];
   391	    const context = new Map<string, any>();
   392	    context.set('PolymorphicRef', PolymorphicRef);
   393	
   394	    const tz = this.#platform.getTimezone();
   395	    const parseDate = (key: string, value: string, padding = '') => {
   396	      lines.push(`${padding}    if (${value} == null || ${value} instanceof Date) {`);
   397	      lines.push(`${padding}      ${key} = ${value};`);
   398	
   399	      if (!tz || tz === 'local') {
   400	        lines.push(`${padding}    } else if (typeof ${value} === 'bigint') {`);

   622	    meta: EntityMetadata<T>,
   623	    prop: EntityProperty<T>,
   624	    context: Map<string, any>,
   625	    level: number,
   626	    path: string[],
   627	    dataKey: string,
   628	    object = prop.object,
   629	  ): string {
   630	    const padding = ' '.repeat(level * 2);
   631	    const nullCond = `entity${path.map(k => this.wrap(k)).join('')} === null`;
   632	    let ret = level === 1 ? '' : '\n';
   633

   635	      ret += `${padding}if (${nullCond}) ret${dataKey} = null;\n`;

import { MikroORM } from '@mikro-orm/sqlite';
import {
  Embeddable,
  Embedded,
  Entity,
  PrimaryKey,
  Property,
  ReflectMetadataProvider,
} from '@mikro-orm/decorators/legacy';

@Embeddable()
class NestedMeta {
  @Property({ nullable: true })
  foo?: string;

  constructor(foo?: string) {
    this.foo = foo;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class ParentMeta {
  @Embedded(() => NestedMeta, { nullable: true })
  nested?: NestedMeta;

  constructor(nested?: NestedMeta) {
    this.nested = nested;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class Identity {
  @Property()
  email!: string;

  @Embedded(() => ParentMeta, { nullable: true })
  parent?: ParentMeta;

  constructor(email: string, parent?: ParentMeta) {
    this.email = email;
    this.parent = parent;
  }
}

@Entity()
class User {
  @PrimaryKey()
  id!: number;

  @Property()
  name!: string;

  @Embedded(() => Identity)
  identity!: Identity;
}

let orm: MikroORM;

beforeAll(async () => {
  orm = await MikroORM.init({
    metadataProvider: ReflectMetadataProvider,
    entities: [User],
    dbName: ':memory:',
    forceUndefined: true,
  });
  await orm.schema.create();
});

afterAll(async () => {
  await orm.close(true);
});

test('debug persist values', async () => {
  const meta = orm.getMetadata().get(User);
  for (const [key, prop] of Object.entries(meta.properties)) {
    console.log(`${key}: kind=${prop.kind}, embedded=${JSON.stringify(prop.embedded)}, object=${prop.object}, persist=${prop.persist}, fieldNames=${JSON.stringify(prop.fieldNames)}`);
  }
  
  // Check what the snapshot generator produces
  const user = new User();
  user.name = 'Test';
  user.identity = new Identity('email@test.com', null);
  
  const snapshot = orm.em.getComparator().prepareEntity(user);
  console.log('Snapshot:', JSON.stringify(snapshot, null, 2));
});
EOF

So the fix needs to be in the snapshot generator: for inline embeddables, intermediate nodes should not be included in the snapshot payload. Only leaf scalar properties (and object/array properties) should be.

Let me look at how this should work. The filter in `getEmbeddedPropertySnapshot` line 676-680:
```ts
.filter(p =>
    p.embedded?.[0] === prop.name &&
    (p.object || p.persist !== false),
)
```

This includes intermediate embeddable nodes because they have `persist !== false`. But they're not real columns. The issue is that they should be filtered out if they're not leaf properties.

Actually, wait. Let me look at the snapshot generation more carefully. The snapshot generator processes `comparableProps` which filters out non-root embedded children. So only the top-level properties (and roots of embedded chains) are processed directly. The recursive calls handle the children.

When `identity_parent` is null, we need to set all its leaf columns to null. Currently, the null case only sets the direct children to null, which for inline embeddables includes intermediate nodes that don't have corresponding columns.

The fix should be: in the null case, if a child is an inline embeddable (not object, not array), we should NOT set `ret[childDataKey] = null` for it. Instead, we should recurse into it to set its own children to null.

But actually, looking at the existing test case `GH3887.sqlite.test.ts`, it has nested inline embeddables and they work fine. Let me check why... In that test, the nested embeddable is not nullable, so the null case is never triggered.

The issue is specifically when a parent inline embeddable is nullable AND set to null. The null case in `getEmbeddedPropertySnapshot` doesn't recurse properly.


For inline embeddables, it sets each direct child to null. But if a child is itself an inline embeddable, we shouldn't set it to null (it's not a column). We should recurse and set its children to null.

import { MikroORM } from '@mikro-orm/sqlite';
import {
  Embeddable,
  Embedded,
  Entity,
  PrimaryKey,
  Property,
  ReflectMetadataProvider,
} from '@mikro-orm/decorators/legacy';

@Embeddable()
class NestedMeta {
  @Property({ nullable: true })
  foo?: string;

  constructor(foo?: string) {
    this.foo = foo;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class ParentMeta {
  @Embedded(() => NestedMeta, { nullable: true })
  nested?: NestedMeta;

  constructor(nested?: NestedMeta) {
    this.nested = nested;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class Identity {
  @Property()
  email!: string;

  @Embedded(() => ParentMeta, { nullable: true })
  parent?: ParentMeta;

  constructor(email: string, parent?: ParentMeta) {
    this.email = email;
    this.parent = parent;
  }
}

@Entity()
class User {
  @PrimaryKey()
  id!: number;

  @Property()
  name!: string;

  @Embedded(() => Identity)
  identity!: Identity;
}

let orm: MikroORM;

beforeAll(async () => {
  orm = await MikroORM.init({
    metadataProvider: ReflectMetadataProvider,
    entities: [User],
    dbName: ':memory:',
  });
  await orm.schema.create();
});

afterAll(async () => {
  await orm.close(true);
});

test('nested inline embeddable with null parent', async () => {
  // Case 1: parent is set, nested is set
  const user1 = new User();
  user1.name = 'Test1';
  user1.identity = new Identity('email1@test.com', new ParentMeta(new NestedMeta('bar')));
  await orm.em.persist(user1).flush();
  
  // Case 2: parent is null
  const user2 = new User();
  user2.name = 'Test2';
  user2.identity = new Identity('email2@test.com', null);
  await orm.em.persist(user2).flush();
  
  // Case 3: parent is set but nested is null
  const user3 = new User();
  user3.name = 'Test3';
  user3.identity = new Identity('email3@test.com', new ParentMeta(null));
  await orm.em.persist(user3).flush();
  
  orm.em.clear();
  
  // Now read them back
  const users = await orm.em.findAll(User);
  
  expect(users[0].identity.parent).toBeDefined();
  expect(users[0].identity.parent!.nested).toBeDefined();
  expect(users[0].identity.parent!.nested!.foo).toBe('bar');
  
  expect(users[1].identity.parent).toBeNull();
  
  expect(users[2].identity.parent).toBeDefined();
  expect(users[2].identity.parent!.nested).toBeNull();
});


For `identity` (prop.nullable = false), `createCond(prop, dataKey, '=== null')`:
- `cond` is `'=== null'`
- `notNull = cond ?? (prop.nullable ? '!= null' : '!== undefined')` = `'=== null'`
- Children:
  - `identity_email`: scalar, `data['identity_email'] === null`
  - `identity_parent`: inline embeddable → recurse with `this.wrap('identity_parent')`

For `identity_parent` (prop.nullable = true), `createCond(identity_parent, `['identity_parent']`, '=== null')`:
- `cond` is `'=== null'`
- `notNull = '=== null'`
- Children:
  - `identity_parent_nested`: inline embeddable → recurse with `this.wrap('identity_parent_nested')`
  - `identity_parent_nested_foo`: scalar → `data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] === null`

So the null check for `identity` would be:
```
data['identity_email'] === null && data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] === null
```

Wait, that's only two conditions. But what about `identity_parent_nested`? It's an intermediate node that gets recursed, and its children are `identity_parent_nested_foo`. So the recursion eventually reaches the leaf scalar.

But wait, in the original code (before my fix), the recursion was:
```
data['identity']['parent']['nested']['foo'] === null
```
which would be wrong because the data is flat.

Now with my fix, it becomes:
```
data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] === null
```
which is correct!

So the `createCond` fix should be correct. But the test still fails because `users[2].identity.parent` is null instead of being defined with `nested: null`.

Let me check the hydration more carefully. The issue might be in `hydrateEmbedded` where it builds the `embeddedData` for inline embeddables.

For User 3, the data from DB:
```
{id: 3, name: 'Test3', identity_email: 'email3@test.com', identity_parent_nested_foo: null}
```

In `hydrateEmbedded` for `identity` (dataKey = `['identity']`):
- Line 428: `if (createCond(prop, dataKey).join(' || '))` → checks if any child is not null
  - After my fix: `data['identity_email'] !== undefined || data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] !== undefined`
  - `identity_email` is 'email3@test.com' → true
  - So we enter the if block

- Line 433-440: build `embeddedData`:
  ```
  {email: data['identity_email'], parent: data['identity_parent']}
  ```
  
  But wait! `data['identity_parent']` doesn't exist in the flat data! The flat data only has `identity_parent_nested_foo`. So `data['identity_parent']` is `undefined`.

  Then `embeddedData` is `{email: 'email3@test.com', parent: undefined}`.

- Line 488-498: recurse into children:
  - `identity_email`: scalar, already handled
  - `identity_parent`: embedded, `childDataKey = this.wrap('identity_parent')` = `['identity_parent']`, calls `hydrateProperty` with `childProp` = `identity_parent` property

  In `hydrateProperty` for `identity_parent`:
  - `dataKey = ['identity_parent']`
  - `hydrateEmbedded` is called
  
  In `hydrateEmbedded` for `identity_parent`:
  - `createCond` checks: `data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] !== undefined` → actually it checks `!= null` since `identity_parent` is nullable. `identity_parent_nested_foo` is null, so this is false.
  - So the condition `createCond(prop, dataKey).join(' || ')` returns false (or empty string? Let me check...)

Actually wait, `createCond` returns an array of conditions. If the only child is `identity_parent_nested_foo` and its value is null, and `cond` is `!= null`, then the condition `data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] != null` is false. So the array is empty? No, the condition is a string like `"data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] != null"`. The `.join(' || ')` would produce that string, and `if ("data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] != null")` is truthy (non-empty string).

Oh! I see the problem now. The `createCond` function returns an array of condition strings. These are joined with ` || ` and then placed inside an `if (...)` statement. But the condition strings themselves are JavaScript expressions like `data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] != null`. When joined, they become `data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] != null`. This is a valid JS expression that evaluates to true/false.

But the problem is: if the array is empty (no children match), then `.join(' || ')` returns an empty string, and `if ()` would be invalid JS!

Wait, let me check what happens when `createCond` returns an empty array. The code at line 428:
```ts
ret.push(`  if (${createCond(prop, dataKey).join(' || ')}) {`);
```

If `createCond` returns `[]`, the join is `''`, so we get `if () {` which is invalid JavaScript. But maybe this case doesn't happen in practice because there's always at least one child?

Actually, for `identity_parent` with `identity_parent_nested_foo` as the only child (the intermediate `identity_parent_nested` is recursed through), the recursion should produce one condition: `data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] != null`. So it should work.

But wait, in my fix for `createCond`, I changed:
```ts
conds.push(...createCond(p, this.wrap(p.name), cond));
```

This recurses with the flat name. But the recursion needs to pass the correct `cond`. Let me trace:

For the null check at line 507:
```ts
ret.push(`  } else if (${createCond(prop, dataKey, '=== null').join(' && ')}) {`);
```

This creates: `data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] === null` (for the nested case).

And for the non-null check at line 428:
```ts
ret.push(`  if (${createCond(prop, dataKey).join(' || ')}) {`);
```

This creates: `data['identity_parent_nested_foo'] != null` (since `identity_parent` is nullable).

So for User 3, `identity_parent_nested_foo` is null, so:
- The "not null" check (line 428) evaluates to false → skip creating the embeddable
- The "is null" check (line 507) evaluates to true → set `entity['identity']['parent'] = null`

That's why `users[2].identity.parent` is null! The hydration thinks the entire `identity_parent` is null just because its leaf column `identity_parent_nested_foo` is null.

But that's wrong! The `identity_parent` should be non-null (it was set to a `ParentMeta` instance with `nested: null`). The leaf column being null should mean the nested property is null, not the parent.

Hmm, but how can we distinguish between:
1. `identity.parent = null` (the whole ParentMeta is null)
2. `identity.parent = new ParentMeta(null)` (ParentMeta exists but nested is null)

In the database, both cases look the same: all leaf columns of `ParentMeta` are null. There's no way to distinguish them just from the database values.

Actually, wait. In case 1, ALL leaf columns under `identity_parent` would be null. In case 2, only some leaf columns might be null (specifically, those under `identity_parent_nested`). But if `ParentMeta` only has one child (`nested`), and `nested` has only `foo`, then both cases produce the same database state: `identity_parent_nested_foo = null`.

But actually, there's a subtle difference: the snapshot generator now correctly handles the null case by recursing. Let me check what snapshot is produced for case 2 vs case 1.

For case 1 (`identity.parent = null`):
- The snapshot generator should produce: `identity_parent_nested_foo = null`

For case 2 (`identity.parent = new ParentMeta(null)`):
- The snapshot generator should produce: `identity_parent_nested_foo = null` too...

So they're indistinguishable at the database level. This is a fundamental issue with nullable inline embeddables. But wait, how does it work for non-nested inline embeddables?

Let me test a simpler case: a single-level inline embeddable with nullable=true.

```ts
@Embeddable()
class Meta {
  @Property({ nullable: true })
  foo?: string;
}

@Entity()
class User {
  @Embedded(() => Meta, { nullable: true })
  meta?: Meta;
}
```

If `user.meta = null`, the DB would have `meta_foo = null`. If `user.meta = new Meta()` (with foo undefined), the DB would also have `meta_foo = null`. Both are stored the same way. When reading back, how does it know whether to set `meta` to null or to `new Meta()`?

The answer might be in the `createCond` logic: if all leaf columns are null, the embeddable is considered null. This is the expected behavior for inline embeddables. There's no way to distinguish between "embedable is null" and "embeddable exists but all its properties are null" because inline embeddables don't have their own column.

So actually, the current behavior might be correct! `users[2].identity.parent` being null when the nested property is null is expected, because all leaf properties of `parent` are null.

But wait, let me re-check my test: User 3 sets `identity.parent = new ParentMeta(null)`. The `ParentMeta` has only one child property `nested` (an inline embeddable). So all leaf columns (`identity_parent_nested_foo`) are null. Therefore, when reading back, `identity.parent` should be null.

But the PR description says "Inline nested embeddable generates wrong column name when parent is null". The original bug was about generating wrong column names, not about the null vs undefined distinction.

Let me go back to the original error: "table user has no column named identity_parent_nested". This was the column name error during insert. My fix to the snapshot generator should have resolved that.

But my test expects `users[2].identity.parent` to be null, and that's what we get. And `users[1].identity.parent` to be null (case 2), which we also get. The test failure is at line 103: `expect(users[2].identity.parent!.nested).toBeNull()`. But `users[2].identity.parent` is null, so we can't access `.nested`.

So the issue is that my test expectation is wrong. For User 3, `parent` is null because all its leaf columns are null. Let me fix the test and also verify the critical behavior:

1. Insert works (no more invalid column error) ✓
2. Reading back works correctly for non-null nested embeddables ✓  
3. Reading back works for null parent ✓
4. Reading back works for null nested ✓

Actually, let me reconsider. Maybe the expected behavior SHOULD be that `parent` is non-null when `parent.nested` is null? But that would require some way to distinguish. Let me check how a simpler case works:

import { MikroORM } from '@mikro-orm/sqlite';
import {
  Embeddable,
  Embedded,
  Entity,
  PrimaryKey,
  Property,
  ReflectMetadataProvider,
} from '@mikro-orm/decorators/legacy';

@Embeddable()
class SimpleMeta {
  @Property({ nullable: true })
  foo?: string;

  constructor(foo?: string) {
    this.foo = foo;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class Identity {
  @Property()
  email!: string;

  @Embedded(() => SimpleMeta, { nullable: true })
  meta?: SimpleMeta;

  constructor(email: string, meta?: SimpleMeta) {
    this.email = email;
    this.meta = meta;
  }
}

@Entity()
class User {
  @PrimaryKey()
  id!: number;

  @Property()
  name!: string;

  @Embedded(() => Identity)
  identity!: Identity;
}

let orm: MikroORM;

beforeAll(async () => {
  orm = await MikroORM.init({
    metadataProvider: ReflectMetadataProvider,
    entities: [User],
    dbName: ':memory:',
  });
  await orm.schema.create();
});

afterAll(async () => {
  await orm.close(true);
});

test('simple inline embeddable with null', async () => {
  // Case 1: meta is set
  const user1 = new User();
  user1.name = 'Test1';
  user1.identity = new Identity('email1@test.com', new SimpleMeta('bar'));
  await orm.em.persist(user1).flush();
  
  // Case 2: meta is null
  const user2 = new User();
  user2.name = 'Test2';
  user2.identity = new Identity('email2@test.com', null);
  await orm.em.persist(user2).flush();
  
  // Case 3: meta is set but foo is undefined
  const user3 = new User();
  user3.name = 'Test3';
  user3.identity = new Identity('email3@test.com', new SimpleMeta());
  await orm.em.persist(user3).flush();
  
  orm.em.clear();
  
  const users = await orm.em.findAll(User);
  
  console.log('User 1 meta:', JSON.stringify(users[0].identity.meta));
  console.log('User 2 meta:', JSON.stringify(users[1].identity.meta));
  console.log('User 3 meta:', JSON.stringify(users[2].identity.meta));
});
EOF

cd /testbed && cat > tests/repro.test.ts << 'EOF'
import { MikroORM } from '@mikro-orm/sqlite';
import {
  Embeddable,
  Embedded,
  Entity,
  PrimaryKey,
  Property,
  ReflectMetadataProvider,
} from '@mikro-orm/decorators/legacy';

@Embeddable()
class NestedMeta {
  @Property({ nullable: true })
  foo?: string;

  constructor(foo?: string) {
    this.foo = foo;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class ParentMeta {
  @Embedded(() => NestedMeta, { nullable: true })
  nested?: NestedMeta;

  constructor(nested?: NestedMeta) {
    this.nested = nested;
  }
}

@Embeddable()
class Identity {
  @Property()
  email!: string;

  @Embedded(() => ParentMeta, { nullable: true })
  parent?: ParentMeta;

  constructor(email: string, parent?: ParentMeta) {
    this.email = email;
    this.parent = parent;
  }
}

@Entity()
class User {
  @PrimaryKey()
  id!: number;

  @Property()
  name!: string;

  @Embedded(() => Identity)
  identity!: Identity;
}

let orm: MikroORM;

beforeAll(async () => {
  orm = await MikroORM.init({
    metadataProvider: ReflectMetadataProvider,
    entities: [User],
    dbName: ':memory:',
  });
  await orm.schema.create();
});

afterAll(async () => {
  await orm.close(true);
});

test('nested inline embeddable with null parent', async () => {
  // Case 1: parent is set, nested is set
  const user1 = new User();
  user1.name = 'Test1';
  user1.identity = new Identity('email1@test.com', new ParentMeta(new NestedMeta('bar')));
  await orm.em.persist(user1).flush();
  
  // Case 2: parent is null
  const user2 = new User();
  user2.name = 'Test2';
  user2.identity = new Identity('email2@test.com', null);
  await orm.em.persist(user2).flush();
  
  // Case 3: parent is set but nested is null
  const user3 = new User();
  user3.name = 'Test3';
  user3.identity = new Identity('email3@test.com', new ParentMeta(null));
  await orm.em.persist(user3).flush();
  
  orm.em.clear();
  
  // Now read them back
  const users = await orm.em.findAll(User);
  
  // Case 1: everything set
  expect(users[0].identity.parent).toBeDefined();
  expect(users[0].identity.parent!.nested).toBeDefined();
  expect(users[0].identity.parent!.nested!.foo).toBe('bar');
  
  // Case 2: parent is null
  expect(users[1].identity.parent).toBeNull();
  
  // Case 3: parent is set but nested is null -> parent should also be null because all leaf columns are null
  expect(users[2].identity.parent).toBeNull();
});
EOF

All 49 tests pass. Now let me clean up the temp test files and think about edge cases.

Let me think about edge cases:

1. **Multiple levels of nesting with nullable at different levels**: Tested with `Identity -> ParentMeta (nullable) -> NestedMeta (nullable) -> foo`. Works.

2. **Mixed object and inline embeddables**: e.g., inline embeddable containing an object embeddable that contains an inline embeddable. Let me check if the `createCond` fix handles this.

3. **Embedded arrays**: The `createCond` function filters out arrays (line 409: `!p.object && !p.array`). Arrays are handled differently.

4. **Polymorphic embeddables**: These use `prop.targetMeta?.polymorphs` and follow a different code path in `hydrateEmbedded`. The `createCond` fix shouldn't affect them because they go through the `prop.object` path first.

Let me also check if my fix to `createCond` could break anything for the object embeddable case. The `createCond` function for object embeddables just returns `data${dataKey} != null` without recursing into children. So the fix only affects the inline case.

But wait, I need to double-check: what about object embeddables that contain inline embeddables? Let me check metadata discovery again... 

Looking at metadata discovery line 1497-1527: when `object` is true (or parent is object), it sets `meta.properties[name].object = true` for all descendants. So if a parent is an object embeddable, all children are treated as object too, even if they would otherwise be inline. This means you can't have an inline embeddable nested inside an object embeddable.

So the recursion in `createCond` for inline embeddables (line 409) is only reached when the current property is inline (not object, not array). And `createCond` for object embeddables just checks the whole object at once.

My fix looks correct.

Now let me also check if there's an issue in the `hydrateEmbedded` function similar to the one in `createCond`. Looking at `hydrateEmbedded` lines 488-498:

```ts
meta.props
    .filter(p => p.embedded?.[0] === prop.name)
    .forEach(childProp => {
        const childDataKey = prop.object ? dataKey + this.wrap(childProp.embedded![1]) : this.wrap(childProp.name);
        ret.push(
            ...hydrateProperty(childProp, prop.object, [...path, childProp.embedded![1]], childDataKey).map(
                l => '  ' + l,
            ),
        );
    });
```

For inline embeddables (`prop.object` is false), `childDataKey = this.wrap(childProp.name)` which uses the flat name. This matches my fix to `createCond` which now also uses `this.wrap(p.name)`.

For object embeddables (`prop.object` is true), `childDataKey = dataKey + this.wrap(childProp.embedded![1])` which uses the path. And `createCond` for object embeddables just checks the whole object, so there's no recursion needed.

Everything looks consistent.

Now let me also check the null case in the non-null branch (lines 636-647 in the updated file). This is what I fixed with `getEmbeddedNullCase`. But wait, I also need to check: does the `hydrateEmbedded` function have a similar null-case issue? Let me look at lines 504-511:

```ts
    ret.push(`  } else if (data${dataKey} === null) {`);
} else {
    ret.push(`  } else if (${createCond(prop, dataKey, '=== null').join(' && ')}) {`);
}

ret.push(`    entity${entityKey} = ${nullVal};`);
ret.push(`  }`);
```

   622	    meta: EntityMetadata<T>,
   623	    prop: EntityProperty<T>,
   624	    context: Map<string, any>,
   625	    padding: string,
   626	    dataKey: string,

   637	        continue;

+  private getEmbeddedNullCase<T>(
+    meta: EntityMetadata<T>,
+    prop: EntityProperty<T>,
+    context: Map<string, any>,
+    padding: string,
+    dataKey: string,
+  ): string {
+    const lines: string[] = [];
+
+    for (const childProp of meta.props) {
+      if (childProp.embedded?.[0] !== prop.name) {
+        continue;
+      }
+
+      // object for JSON embeddable, or persist check
+      if (!childProp.object && childProp.persist === false) {
+        continue;
+      }
+
+      const childDataKey = meta.embeddable || prop.object
+        ? dataKey + this.wrap(childProp.embedded![1])
+        : this.wrap(childProp.name);
+
+      if (childProp.kind === ReferenceKind.EMBEDDED && !childProp.object && !childProp.array) {
+        // inline nested embeddable: recurse to set its leaf properties to null
+        lines.push(this.getEmbeddedNullCase(meta, childProp, context, padding + '  ', childDataKey));
+      } else {
+        lines.push(`${padding}  ret${childDataKey} = null;`);
+      }
+    }
+
+    return lines.join('\n') + (lines.length ? '\n' : '');
+  }
